<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Bill O'Reilly (political commentator)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>William James</b> "<b>Bill</b>" <b>O'Reilly Jr.</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fyr_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-fyr-1">[1]</a></sup> (born September 10, 1949<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fyr_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-fyr-1">[1]</a></sup>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Presenter" title="Presenter">television host</a>, author, journalist, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syndicated_columnist" title="Syndicated columnist">syndicated columnist</a>, and political commentator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> He is the host of the <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">political commentary</a> program <i><a href="/wiki/The_O%27Reilly_Factor" title="The O'Reilly Factor">The O'Reilly Factor</a></i> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> During the late 1970s and 1980s, he worked as a news reporter for various local television stations in the United States and eventually for <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a>. From 1989 to 1995, he was anchor of the news magazine program <i><a href="/wiki/Inside_Edition" title="Inside Edition">Inside Edition</a></i>.</p>
<p>O'Reilly is widely considered a <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> commentator,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> although some of his positions diverge from conservative orthodoxy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> O'Reilly is registered as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_of_New_York" title="Independence Party of New York">Independence Party of New York</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and was formerly registered as a <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and characterizes himself as a <a href="/wiki/Traditionalist_conservatism" title="Traditionalist conservatism">traditionalist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-npr-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> O'Reilly is the author of over a dozen <a href="#Books_by_O.27Reilly">books</a>, and hosted <i><a href="/wiki/The_Radio_Factor" title="The Radio Factor">The Radio Factor</a></i> until early 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>O'Reilly was born on September 10, 1949, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_Presbyterian_Hospital" title="Columbia Presbyterian Hospital">Columbia Presbyterian Hospital</a> in New York City, to parents William James, Sr., (deceased) and Winifred Angela (Drake) O'Reilly, from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brooklyn,_New_York" title="Brooklyn, New York">Brooklyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teaneck,_New_Jersey" title="Teaneck, New Jersey">Teaneck</a>, New Jersey, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> O'Reilly is of Irish descent, along with a small amount of English (<a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States" title="Colonial history of the United States">Colonial American</a>) ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Some of his father's ancestors lived in <a href="/wiki/County_Cavan" title="County Cavan">County Cavan</a>, Ireland, since the early eighteenth century, and on his mother's side, he has ancestry from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The O'Reilly family lived in a small apartment in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lee,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Lee, New Jersey">Fort Lee</a>, New Jersey, when their son was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1951 his family moved to <a href="/wiki/Levittown,_New_York" title="Levittown, New York">Levittown</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> O'Reilly has a sister, Janet.</p>
<p>He attended St. Brigid parochial school in <a href="/wiki/Westbury,_New_York" title="Westbury, New York">Westbury</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chaminade_High_School" title="Chaminade High School">Chaminade High School</a>, a private Catholic boys high school in <a href="/wiki/Mineola,_New_York" title="Mineola, New York">Mineola</a>. His father wanted him to attend Chaminade, but Bill wanted to attend <a href="/wiki/W._Tresper_Clarke_High_School" title="W. Tresper Clarke High School">W. Tresper Clarke High School</a>, the public school most of his closest friends would attend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Bill O'Reilly played <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Little_League" title="Little League">Little League</a> baseball and was the goalie on the Chaminade varsity hockey team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> During his high school years, O'Reilly met future pop-singer icon <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a>, whom O'Reilly described as a "hoodlum". O'Reilly recollected in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kay_(sports_broadcaster)" title="Michael Kay (sports broadcaster)">Michael Kay</a> on the <a href="/wiki/YES_Network" title="YES Network">YES Network</a> show <i>CenterStage</i> that Joel "was in the <a href="/wiki/Hicksville,_New_York" title="Hicksville, New York">Hicksville</a> section—the same age as me—and he was a hood. He used to slick it [his hair] back like this. And we knew him, because his guys would smoke and this and that, and we were more jocks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.yesnetwork.com_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-web.yesnetwork.com-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>After graduating from high school in 1967, O'Reilly attended <a href="/wiki/Marist_College" title="Marist College">Marist College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Poughkeepsie,_New_York" title="Poughkeepsie, New York">Poughkeepsie</a>, New York, his father's choice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> While at Marist, O'Reilly played punter in the <a href="/wiki/National_Club_Football_Association" title="National Club Football Association">National Club Football Association</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and was also a writer for the school's newspaper, <i>The Circle</i>. An honors student, he majored in history. He spent his junior year of college abroad, attending <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Mary,_University_of_London" title="Queen Mary, University of London">Queen Mary College</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> O'Reilly received his bachelor of arts degree in history in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_News_Bio_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_News_Bio-26">[26]</a></sup> He played <a href="/wiki/Semi-professional" title="Semi-professional">semi-professional</a> baseball during this time as a pitcher for the New York Monarchs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> After graduating from Marist College, O'Reilly moved to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, where he taught <a href="/wiki/English_studies" title="English studies">English</a> and history at <a href="/wiki/Monsignor_Edward_Pace_High_School" title="Monsignor Edward Pace High School">Monsignor Pace High School</a> from 1970 to 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> O'Reilly returned to school in 1973<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and earned a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_of_arts" title="Master of arts">master of arts</a> degree in <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_journalism" title="Broadcast journalism">broadcast journalism</a> from <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_News_Bio_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_News_Bio-26">[26]</a></sup> While attending Boston University, he was a reporter and columnist for various local newspapers and alternative news weeklies, including the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phoenix_(newspaper)" title="The Phoenix (newspaper)">Boston Phoenix</a></i>, and did an <a href="/wiki/Internship" title="Internship">internship</a> in the newsroom of <a href="/wiki/WBZ-TV" title="WBZ-TV">WBZ-TV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> During his time at BU, O'Reilly also was a classmate of future radio talk show host <a href="/wiki/Howard_Stern" title="Howard Stern">Howard Stern</a>, whom O'Reilly noticed because Stern was the only student on campus taller than he was.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.yesnetwork.com_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-web.yesnetwork.com-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1995, having established himself as a national media personality, O'Reilly was accepted to <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_School_of_Government" title="John F. Kennedy School of Government">John F. Kennedy School of Government</a>; he received a mid-career <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_of_public_administration" title="Master of public administration">master of public administration</a> degree in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_News_Bio_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_News_Bio-26">[26]</a></sup> At Harvard, he was a student of <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Kalb" title="Marvin Kalb">Marvin Kalb</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting_career">Broadcasting career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<p>O'Reilly's early television news career included reporting and anchoring positions at <a href="/wiki/WNEP-TV" title="WNEP-TV">WNEP-TV</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scranton,_Pennsylvania" title="Scranton, Pennsylvania">Scranton</a>, Pennsylvania, where he also reported the weather. At <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WFAA-TV" title="WFAA-TV">WFAA-TV</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, O'Reilly was awarded the Dallas Press Club Award for excellence in <a href="/wiki/Investigative_journalism" title="Investigative journalism">investigative reporting</a>. He then moved to <a href="/wiki/KMGH-TV" title="KMGH-TV">KMGH-TV</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, where he won a local <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> for his coverage of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skyjacking" title="Skyjacking">skyjacking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FoxBio1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FoxBio1-32">[32]</a></sup> O'Reilly also worked for <a href="/wiki/KATU" title="KATU">KATU</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a>, Oregon, <a href="/wiki/WFSB" title="WFSB">WFSB</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford</a>, Connecticut, and WNEV-TV (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHDH-TV" title="WHDH-TV">WHDH-TV</a>) in Boston.</p>
<p>In 1980 O'Reilly anchored the local news-feature program <i>7:30 Magazine</i> at <a href="/wiki/WCBS-TV" title="WCBS-TV">WCBS-TV</a> in New York. Soon after, as a WCBS News anchor and correspondent, he won his second local Emmy, for an investigation of corrupt city marshals. In 1982 he was promoted to the network as a <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> correspondent.</p>
<p>For CBS, O'Reilly covered the wars in <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> on location, and in the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> from his base in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina. O'Reilly left CBS over a dispute concerning the uncredited use in a report by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Schieffer" title="Bob Schieffer">Bob Schieffer</a> of footage of a riot in response to the military junta's surrender, shot by O'Reilly's crew in Buenos Aires shortly after the conclusion of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motherjones1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-motherjones1-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1986, O'Reilly joined <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> as a correspondent. He had delivered a eulogy for his friend Joe Spencer, an ABC News correspondent who died in a helicopter crash on January 22, 1986, en route to covering the <a href="/wiki/Hormel" title="Hormel">Hormel</a> meatpacker strike. ABC News president <a href="/wiki/Roone_Arledge" title="Roone Arledge">Roone Arledge</a>, who attended Spencer's funeral, decided to hire O'Reilly after hearing the eulogy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> At ABC, O'Reilly hosted daytime news briefs that previewed stories to be reported on the day's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_News_with_Diane_Sawyer" title="World News with Diane Sawyer">World News Tonight</a></i> and worked as a general assignment reporter for ABC News programs, including <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nightline_(U.S._news_program)" title="Nightline (U.S. news program)">Nightline</a></i>, and <i>World News Tonight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inside_Edition"><i>Inside Edition</i></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Inside_Edition" title="Inside Edition">Inside Edition</a></div>
<p>In 1989 O'Reilly joined the nationally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_syndication" title="Television syndication">syndicated</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_World" title="King World">King World</a> (now <a href="/wiki/CBS_Television_Distribution" title="CBS Television Distribution">CBS Television Distribution</a>)-produced <i><a href="/wiki/Inside_Edition" title="Inside Edition">Inside Edition</a></i>, a tabloid-gossip television program in competition with <i><a href="/wiki/A_Current_Affair_(U.S._TV_series)" title="A Current Affair (U.S. TV series)">A Current Affair</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_News_Bio_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_News_Bio-26">[26]</a></sup> He became the program's anchor three weeks into its run, after the termination of original anchor <a href="/wiki/David_Frost" title="David Frost">David Frost</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In addition to being one of the first American broadcasters to cover the dismantling of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>, O'Reilly obtained the first exclusive interview with murderer <a href="/wiki/Joel_Steinberg" title="Joel Steinberg">Joel Steinberg</a> and was the first television host from a national current affairs program on the scene of the <a href="/wiki/1992_Los_Angeles_riots" title="1992 Los Angeles riots">1992 Los Angeles riots</a>.</p>
<p>Former <a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC News</a> and <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> anchor <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Norville" title="Deborah Norville">Deborah Norville</a> replaced O'Reilly on <i>Inside Edition</i> in 1995; O'Reilly had expressed a desire to quit the show in July 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> He then enrolled in September 1995 at the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_School_of_Government" title="John F. Kennedy School of Government">John F. Kennedy School of Government</a> at Harvard University,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> where he received a master's degree in public administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fox_News_Bio_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_News_Bio-26">[26]</a></sup> His graduate thesis, which he researched in Singapore, was titled <i>Theory of Coerced Drug Rehabilitation</i>. In his thesis, O'Reilly asserted that supervised mandatory drug rehabilitation would reduce crime, based on the rate of prison return for criminals in <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> who enrolled in such a program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_O.27Reilly_Factor"><i>The O'Reilly Factor</i></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_O%27Reilly_Factor" title="The O'Reilly Factor">The O'Reilly Factor</a></div>
<p>After Harvard, he was hired by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ailes" title="Roger Ailes">Roger Ailes</a>, chairman and CEO of the then startup <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a>, to anchor <i>The O'Reilly Report</i> in October 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oreilly_on_rolling_stone_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-oreilly_on_rolling_stone-41">[41]</a></sup> The show was renamed <i><a href="/wiki/The_O%27Reilly_Factor" title="The O'Reilly Factor">The O'Reilly Factor</a></i>, after O'Reilly's friend and branding expert <a href="/wiki/John_Tantillo" title="John Tantillo">John Tantillo</a>'s remarks upon the "O'Reilly Factor" in any of the stories O'Reilly told.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oreilly_on_rolling_stone_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-oreilly_on_rolling_stone-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The program is routinely the highest-rated show of the three major U.S. <a href="/wiki/24-hour_news_cycle" title="24-hour news cycle">24-hour</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_cable_news" title="United States cable news">cable news</a> television channels and began the trend toward more opinion-oriented prime-time cable news programming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_ratings_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA_ratings-44">[44]</a></sup> The show is taped late in the afternoon at a studio in New York City and airs every weekday on the Fox News Channel at 8:00 p.m. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_Eastern_Standard_Time_Zone" title="North American Eastern Standard Time Zone">Eastern Time</a> and is rebroadcast at 11:00 p.m.</p>
<p>Until early 2009, O'Reilly hosted a radio program that had more than 3.26 million listeners and was carried by more than 400 radio stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> According to the talk radio industry publication <i><a href="/wiki/Talkers_Magazine" title="Talkers Magazine">Talkers Magazine</a></i>, O'Reilly was No. 11 on the "Heavy Hundred", a list of the 100 most important talk show hosts in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Conservative Internet news site <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NewsMax" title="NewsMax">NewsMax</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "Top 25 Talk Radio Host" list selected O'Reilly to the No. 2 spot as most influential host in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>O'Reilly's life and career have not been without controversy. <a href="/wiki/Progressivism_in_the_United_States" title="Progressivism in the United States">Progressive</a> media watchdog organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Media_Matters_for_America" title="Media Matters for America">Media Matters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fairness_and_Accuracy_in_Reporting" title="Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting">Fairness and Accuracy in Reporting</a> have criticized O'Reilly's reporting on a variety of issues, accusing him of distorting facts and using misleading or erroneous statistics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fair.org_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-fair.org-48">[48]</a></sup> In 2008, citing numerous inaccuracies in his reporting, MediaMatters for America awarded O'Reilly its first annual "Misinformer of the Year" award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, O'Reilly accused the <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way of America</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> of failing to deliver millions of dollars in donated money, raised by the organizations in the name of the disaster, to the families of those killed in the attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> O'Reilly reported that the organizations misrepresented their intentions for the money being raised by not distributing all of the 9/11 relief fund to the victims. Actor <a href="/wiki/George_Clooney" title="George Clooney">George Clooney</a> responded, accusing O'Reilly of misstating facts and harming the relief effort by inciting "panic" among potential donors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beginning in 2005, O'Reilly periodically denounced <a href="/wiki/George_Tiller" title="George Tiller">George Tiller</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>-based physician who specialized in second- and third-trimester abortions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> often referring to him as "Tiller the baby killer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Tiller was <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_George_Tiller" title="Assassination of George Tiller">murdered</a> on May 31, 2009, by Scott Roeder, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-abortion" title="Anti-abortion">anti-abortion</a> activist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Critics such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salon.com" title="Salon.com">Salon.com</a>'s Gabriel Winant have asserted that O'Reilly's anti-Tiller rhetoric helped to create an atmosphere of violence around the doctor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Jay Bookman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlanta_Journal-Constitution" title="The Atlanta Journal-Constitution">The Atlanta Journal-Constitution</a></i> wrote that O'Reilly "clearly went overboard in his condemnation and demonization of Tiller", but added that it was "irresponsible to link O'Reilly" to Tiller's murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> O'Reilly has responded to the criticism by saying "no backpedaling here ... every single thing we said about Tiller was true."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 2007, researchers from the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_University" title="Indiana University">Indiana University</a> School of Journalism published a report that analyzed O'Reilly's "Talking Points Memo" segment. Using analysis techniques developed in the 1930s by the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Propaganda_Analysis" title="Institute for Propaganda Analysis">Institute for Propaganda Analysis</a>, the study concluded that O'Reilly used propaganda, frequently engaged in <a href="/wiki/Name_calling" title="Name calling">name calling</a>, and consistently cast non-Americans as threats and never "in the role of victim or hero."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> O'Reilly responded, asserting that "the terms 'conservative', 'liberal', '<a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left</a>', '<a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right</a>', '<a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a>', 'traditional' and '<a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a>' were considered name-calling if they were associated with a problem or social ill." The study's authors said that those terms were only considered name-calling when linked to derogatory qualifiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimes-Conway_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-Conway-60">[60]</a></sup> Fox News producer Ron Mitchell wrote an op-ed in which he accused the study's authors of seeking to manipulate their research to fit a predetermined outcome. Mitchell argued that by using tools developed for examining propaganda, the researchers presupposed that O'Reilly propagandized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>O'Reilly was the main inspiration for comedian <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert_(character)" title="Stephen Colbert (character)">satirical character</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i>, which featured Colbert in a "full-dress parody" of <i>The O'Reilly Factor</i>. On the show, Colbert referred to O'Reilly as "Papa Bear".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> O'Reilly and Colbert exchanged appearances on each other's shows in January 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Speaking on ABC's <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> on March 18, 2003, O'Reilly promised that "[i]f the Americans go in and overthrow <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> and it's clean [of weapons of mass destruction] ... I will apologize to the nation, and I will not trust the Bush administration again."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In another appearance on the same program on February 10, 2004, O'Reilly responded to repeated requests for him to honor his pledge: "My analysis was wrong and I'm sorry. I was wrong. I'm not pleased about it at all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> With regard to never again trusting the current U.S. government, he said, "I am much more skeptical of the Bush administration now than I was at that time."</p>
<p>On May 10, 2008, O'Reilly was presented with the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Television_Arts_and_Sciences" title="National Academy of Television Arts and Sciences">National Academy of Television Arts and Sciences</a> Governors' Award at an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emmy" title="Emmy">Emmy</a> awards show dinner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disputed_claims">Disputed claims</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="George_de_Mohrenschildt_claim">George de Mohrenschildt claim</span></h4>
<p>In his bestselling 2013 book <i><a href="/wiki/Killing_Kennedy" title="Killing Kennedy">Killing Kennedy</a></i> and on <i>Fox and Friends</i>, O'Reilly claimed he was knocking at the front door of <a href="/wiki/George_de_Mohrenschildt" title="George de Mohrenschildt">George de Mohrenschildt</a>'s daughter's home at the moment Mohrenschildt committed suicide and that he heard the shotgun blast:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>In March of 1977, a young television reporter at WFAA in Dallas began looking into the Kennedy assassination. As part of his reporting, he sought an interview with the shadowy Russian professor who had befriended the Oswalds upon their arrival in Dallas in 1962. The reporter traced George de Mohrenschildt to Palm Beach, Florida and travelled there to confront him. At the time de Mohrenschildt had been called to testify before a congressional committee looking into the events of November, 1963. As the reporter knocked on the door of de Mohrenschildt’s daughter’s home, he heard the shotgun blast [Emphasis added] that marked the suicide of the Russian, assuring that his relationship with Lee Harvey Oswald would never be fully understood. By the way, that reporter’s name is Bill O’Reilly.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>This claim has been disproven by former <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> editor Jefferson Morley, who cites audio recordings made by <a href="/wiki/Gaeton_Fonzi" title="Gaeton Fonzi">Gaeton Fonzi</a> indicating O'Reilly was not present in Florida on the day of Mohrenschildt's suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jfkf_JFKf_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-jfkf_JFKf-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mone_Bill_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-mone_Bill-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="War_coverage_claims">War coverage claims</span></h4>
<p>On February 19, 2015, <a href="/wiki/David_Corn" title="David Corn">David Corn</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Mother_Jones_(magazine)" title="Mother Jones (magazine)">Mother Jones</a></i> broke a story reporting a collection of inconsistencies of O'Reilly when recalling his experience covering the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motherjones1_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-motherjones1-34">[34]</a></sup> On April 17, 2013, O'Reilly said on his show "I was in a situation one time, in a war zone in Argentina, in the Falklands, (...)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In his book <i>The No Spin Zone</i>, he wrote "You know that I am not easily shocked. I've reported on the ground in active war zones from El Salvador to the Falklands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nospin-book_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-nospin-book-70">[70]</a></sup> On a 2004 column on his website he wrote: "Having survived a combat situation in Argentina during the Falklands war, I know that life-and-death decisions are made in a flash."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Corn claimed O'Reilly was not in the Falklands, but in Buenos Aires and that no American journalist was in the Islands during the conflict. Also he pointed out that according to O'Reilly's own book <i>The No Spin Zone</i>, he arrived in Buenos Aires soon before the war ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motherjones1_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-motherjones1-34">[34]</a></sup> On February 20, 2015, O'Reilly said on his show "David Corn, a liar, says that I exaggerated situations in the Falklands War" and that he never said he was on the Falkland Islands. O'Reilly went on to describe his experience in a riot in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> the day Argentina surrendered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nati_Bill_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-nati_Bill-72">[72]</a></sup> David Corn replied that they didn't claim O'Reilly "exaggerated" but rather that there were contradictions between his accounts and the factual record, and that the 2013 clip from his show proves O'Reilly did in fact say he was on the Falklands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-motherjones2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-motherjones2-73">[73]</a></sup> David Corn told <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> “The question is whether Bill O’Reilly was stating the truth when he repeatedly said that Argentine soldiers used real bullets and fired into the crowd of civilians and many were killed.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2015 Ignacio Medrano-Carbo stated that he was the camerman O'Reilly referred to and that at no time was he knocked down or bleeding from the ear. Sound man Roberto Moreno corroborates this fact. Medrano also stated "I do not even recall Mr. O'Reilly being near me when I shot all that footage nor after I left the unrest at Plaza de Mayo that evening."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 2009, during an interview he said he covered the riots in Buenos Aires on the day Argentina surrendered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interview2009-falklands_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-interview2009-falklands-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>During an interview with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Blaze" title="The Blaze">The Blaze</a>, O'Reilly said "And if that moron [Corn] doesn’t think it was a war zone in Buenos Aires, then he’s even dumber than I think he is."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> This characterization by O'Reilly was disputed by former CBS colleague <a href="/wiki/Eric_Engberg" title="Eric Engberg">Eric Engberg</a> who was in Buenos Aires at the time and challenged his (O'Reilly) description of the riot as a "combat situation". Engberg went on to say it was a moderate riot and he heard no “shots fired” and saw no “ambulances or tanks” in the streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The following week O’Reilly contradicted Engberg’s claims presenting archived CBS video of the riot that ensued after <a href="/wiki/Argentine_surrender_in_the_Falklands_War" title="Argentine surrender in the Falklands War">Argentine’s surrender</a>. The video appears to show riot police firing tear gas and plastic bullets toward the crowd, additionally former NBC bureau chief <a href="/wiki/Don_Browne" title="Don Browne">Don Browne</a> referred to the riot as an “intense situation”, with many people hurt and <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a> in the streets of Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fallout from the coverage generated by the questioning of O'Reilly's Falklands War coverage saw claims made by O'Reilly regarding his reporting in El Salvador and Northern Ireland questioned. Writing in his 2013 book <i>Keep it Pithy</i>, O'Reilly stated: "I've seen soldiers gun down unarmed civilians in Latin America, Irish terrorists kill and maim their fellow citizens in Belfast with bombs." In 2005 O'Reilly claimed to have "seen guys gun down nuns in El Salvador" and in 2012 said "I saw nuns get shot in the back of the head". O'Reilly and Fox News clarified that he had been shown images of the murdered nuns and Irish bombings but was not an eyewitness in either case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span></h3>
<p>O'Reilly wrote a weekly syndicated newspaper column through <a href="/wiki/Creators_Syndicate" title="Creators Syndicate">Creators Syndicate</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> that appeared in numerous newspapers, including the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> He discontinued the column at the end of 2013.</p>
<p>O'Reilly made cameo appearances in the films <i><a href="/wiki/An_American_Carol" title="An American Carol">An American Carol</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Man_2" title="Iron Man 2">Iron Man 2</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers:_Dark_of_the_Moon" title="Transformers: Dark of the Moon">Transformers: Dark of the Moon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flic_Bill_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-flic_Bill-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vani_Does_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-vani_Does-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_AnAm_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdb_AnAm-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views_and_public_perception">Political views and public perception</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_views_of_Bill_O%27Reilly" title="Political views of Bill O'Reilly">Political views of Bill O'Reilly</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="650" height="305" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bill_O%27Reilly_at_the_World_Affairs_Council_of_Philadelphia_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
O'Reilly in Philadelphia, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On <i>The O'Reilly Factor</i> and on his former talk-radio program, Bill O'Reilly has focused on news and commentary related to politics and culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sandiego_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-sandiego-88">[88]</a></sup> O'Reilly has long said that he does not identify with any political ideology, writing in his book <i>The O'Reilly Factor</i> that the reader "might be wondering whether I'm <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarian</a>, or exactly what ... See, I don't want to fit any of those labels, because I believe that the truth doesn't have labels. When I see corruption, I try to expose it. When I see exploitation, I try to fight it. That's my political position."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> On December 6, 2000, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i> in New York reported, however, that he had been registered with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican Party</a> in the state of New York since 1994. When questioned about this, he said that he was not aware of it and says he registered as an independent after the interview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> During a broadcast of <i>The Radio Factor</i>, O'Reilly said that there was no option to register as an independent voter; however, there was in fact a box marked "I do not wish to enroll in party."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Despite his being registered as an Independence Party member, many view him as a conservative figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sandiego_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-sandiego-88">[88]</a></sup> A February 2009 Pew Research poll found that 66% of his television viewers identify themselves as conservative, 24% moderate, and 3% liberal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> A November 2008 poll by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zogby_International" title="Zogby International">Zogby International</a> found that O'Reilly was the second most trusted news personality, after <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2003 interview with <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gross" title="Terry Gross">Terry Gross</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a>, O'Reilly said:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I'm not a political guy in the sense that I embrace an ideology. To this day I'm an independent thinker, an independent voter, I'm a registered independent ... [T]here are certain fundamental things that this country was founded upon that I respect and don't want changed. That separates me from the secularists who want a complete overhaul of how the country is run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-npr-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On a September 2007 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Radio_Factor" title="The Radio Factor">The Radio Factor</a></i>, while having a discussion about race with fellow Fox News commentator and author <a href="/wiki/Juan_Williams" title="Juan Williams">Juan Williams</a> about a meal he shared with <a href="/wiki/Al_Sharpton" title="Al Sharpton">Al Sharpton</a>, O'Reilly said "You know when Sharpton and I walked in, it was like... big commotion and everything. But everybody was very nice. And I couldn't get over the fact that there was no difference between <a href="/wiki/Sylvia%27s_Restaurant_of_Harlem" title="Sylvia's Restaurant of Harlem">Sylvia's restaurant</a> and any other restaurant in New York City. I mean, it was exactly the same, even though it's run by blacks, primarily black patronship." He commented that no one in Sylvia's was "screaming 'M'Fer, I want more iced tea.'" He further added, "I think that black Americans are starting to think more and more for themselves, getting away from the Sharptons and the <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Jackson" title="Jesse Jackson">Jacksons</a> and people trying to lead them into a race-based culture. They're just trying to figure it out. 'Look, I can make it. If I work hard and get educated, I can make it.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The statement drew criticism from a number of places. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roland_S._Martin" title="Roland S. Martin">Roland S. Martin</a> of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> said that the notion that black people are just now starting to value education is "ridiculous" and that the notion that black people let Sharpton or Jackson think for them is "nuts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Media_Matters_for_America" title="Media Matters for America">Media Matters for America</a> covered the story on a number of occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> O'Reilly responded, saying, "It was an attempt to tell the radio audience that there is no difference—black, white, we're all Americans. The stereotypes they see on television are not true" and also called out Media Matters, claiming that "Media Matters distorted the entire conversation and implied I was <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racist</a> for condemning racism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Juan Williams said the criticism of O'Reilly was "rank dishonesty" and that the original comments "had nothing to do with racist ranting by anybody except by these idiots at CNN." Williams went on to say it was "frustrating" that the media try to criticize anyone who wanted to have an honest discussion about race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smeared_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-smeared-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>O'Reilly has long said that his inspiration for speaking up for average Americans is his working-class roots. He has pointed to his boyhood home in <a href="/wiki/Levittown,_New_York" title="Levittown, New York">Levittown, New York</a>, as a credential. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, O'Reilly's mother said that her family lived in <a href="/wiki/Westbury,_New_York" title="Westbury, New York">Westbury</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifeoforeilly_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-lifeoforeilly-100">[100]</a></sup> which is a few miles from Levittown. Citing this interview, then <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberal</a> talk-show pundit <a href="/wiki/Al_Franken" title="Al Franken">Al Franken</a> accused O'Reilly of distorting his background to create a more working-class image. O'Reilly countered that <i>The Washington Post</i> misquoted his mother<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and that his mother still lives in his childhood home, which was built by William Levitt. O'Reilly placed a copy of the house's mortgage on his website; the mortgage shows a Levittown postal address.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> O'Reilly has also said, "You don't come from any lower than I came from on an economic scale"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and that his father, a currency accountant for an oil company,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Facts_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Facts-104">[104]</a></sup> "never earned more than $35,000 a year in his life." O'Reilly responded that his father's $35,000 income only came at the end of his long career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>O'Reilly was married to Maureen E. McPhilmy, a public relations executive. They met in 1992, and their wedding took place in St. Brigid Parish of Westbury on November 2, 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> They have a daughter, Madeline (born 1998), and a son, Spencer (born 2003).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The couple separated on April 2, 2010, and were divorced on September 1, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Each currently resides in suburban <a href="/wiki/Manhasset,_New_York" title="Manhasset, New York">Manhasset, New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_harassment_and_extortion_lawsuits">Sexual harassment and extortion lawsuits <span id="Sexual_harassment_lawsuit"></span></span></h3>
<p>On October 13, 2004, O'Reilly sued Andrea Mackris, a former producer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_O%27Reilly_Factor" title="The O'Reilly Factor">The O'Reilly Factor</a></i>, with extortion charges, alleging that she had threatened a lawsuit unless he paid her more than $60 million. Subsequently, that day, Mackris sued O'Reilly for <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, seeking $60 million in damages. Her lawsuit alleged two types of legally-cognizable sexual harassment claims that are not based upon physical contact: <i><a href="/wiki/Quid_pro_quo" title="Quid pro quo">quid pro quo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hostile_work_environment" title="Hostile work environment">hostile work environment</a></i>. In her lawsuit, she filed a 22-page complaint with the Supreme Court of the State of New York,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mackris_complaint_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mackris_complaint-111">[111]</a></sup> including quotations from alleged explicit phone conversations between herself and O'Reilly in which he "advised her to use a vibrator and told her about sexual fantasies involving her",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS-112">[112]</a></sup> and an allegation that he threatened that if she reported his behavior, "Roger Ailes...will go after you...Ailes operates behind the scenes, strategizes, and makes things happen so that one day BAM! The person gets what's coming to them but never sees it coming." On October 15, 2004, Fox sought judicial permission to fire Mackris, but she was never dismissed. On October 19, 2004, Mackris filed an amended complaint seeking further damages for illegal retaliatory actions by O'Reilly, Fox News, and the <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation" title="News Corporation">News Corporation</a>-owned newspaper the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSG_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSG-113">[113]</a></sup> On October 28, 2004, O'Reilly and Mackris reached an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out-of-court_settlement" title="Out-of-court settlement">out-of-court settlement</a> and dropped all charges against each other. The terms of the agreement are confidential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-settleoct28_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-settleoct28-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Ailes was the subject of a sexual harassment lawsuit filed by former Fox News coworker <a href="/wiki/Gretchen_Carlson" title="Gretchen Carlson">Gretchen Carlson</a>, O'Reilly said in July 2016 that Ailes was a "target" as a "famous, powerful or wealthy person" and called him the "best boss I ever had."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> After Ailes was fired and the network settled the lawsuit with Carlson, O'Reilly declined to comment further, saying that " for once in my life, I’m going to keep my big mouth shut."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after Ailes was fired, Fox News settled yet another sexual harassment claim against O'Reilly for a sum reported to be in the high six figures. The settlement was reached with former Fox host <a href="/wiki/Juliet_Huddy" title="Juliet Huddy">Juliet Huddy</a>, who alleged that O'Reilly pursued a romantic relationship with her, made lewd remarks, including a telephone call during which he appeared to be masturbating, and tried to have her fired when she rejected his advances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Legal fees in this case were settled and paid for by Fox News.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2016, former Fox host <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Tantaros" title="Andrea Tantaros">Andrea Tantaros</a> filed a sexual harassment lawsuit against Fox News, claiming that O'Reilly made sexually suggestive comments to her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_violence_accusation_from_daughter">Domestic violence accusation from daughter</span></h3>
<p>In May 2015, court transcripts from O’Reilly's custody trial with ex-wife Maureen McPhilmy revealed signs of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> within the household—O’Reilly's daughter testified to a forensic examiner that she witnessed O’Reilly <a href="/wiki/Choking" title="Choking">choking</a> McPhilmy and dragging her down the stairs of their home by her neck, apparently unaware that the daughter was watching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insider_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-insider-122">[122]</a></sup> In light of the allegation, O’Reilly issued a statement through his attorney describing the account as "100% false" and declined to comment further in order “to respect the court-mandated confidentiality put in place to protect [his] children”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insider_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-insider-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In February 2016, O'Reilly lost a bid for custody of both of his children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_disputes">Public disputes</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ludacris">Ludacris</span></h3>
<p>On August 27, 2002, O'Reilly called for all Americans to boycott <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> products,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[125]</a></sup> saying that <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>' (then appearing in ads for Pepsi) lyrics glamorize a "life of guns, violence, drugs and disrespect of women."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The next day, O'Reilly reported that Pepsi had fired Ludacris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three years later, Ludacris referenced O'Reilly in the song "<a href="/wiki/Number_One_Spot" title="Number One Spot">Number One Spot</a>" with the lyrics "Respected highly, hi, Mr. O'Reilly/Hope all is well, kiss the plaintiff and the wifey.", which alludes to his well publicized sexual harassment suit while married. In an interview with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RadarOnline.com" title="RadarOnline.com">RadarOnline.com</a> in 2010, Ludacris stated that the two had made amends after a conversation at a charity event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joy_Behar.2FWhoopi_Goldberg">Joy Behar/Whoopi Goldberg</span></h3>
<p>On October 14, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Joy_Behar" title="Joy Behar">Joy Behar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whoopi_Goldberg" title="Whoopi Goldberg">Whoopi Goldberg</a> walked off the set of <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i> after they both disagreed with statements made by O'Reilly, specifically O'Reilly's statement "Muslims killed us on 9/11."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Goldberg stated O'Reilly should be more specific than just labeling Muslims. O'Reilly defended his statement citing the lack of specificity when describing attacks by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. O'Reilly later explained on his show that the statement was valid when he said "Of course, what I said is absolutely true, but is insensitive to some. In a perfect world you always say Muslim terrorists killed us, but at this point I thought that was common knowledge. I guess I was wrong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a> disagreed with O'Reilly's defense of the World War II comparison stating that describing a religion is not the same as describing a country. Walters would go on to say, "We should be able to have discussion without ... walking off stage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Former host and progressive commentator <a href="/wiki/Rosie_O%27Donnell" title="Rosie O'Donnell">Rosie O'Donnell</a> stated on her radio program that the incident was an example of what she viewed as regular hateful statements. O'Reilly responded by citing O'Donnell's earlier statement about claiming the threat from radical Christianity is similar to that of radical Islam.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-Defamation_League">Anti-Defamation League</span></h3>
<p>On December 8, 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> (ADL) sent O'Reilly a letter criticizing him for making remarks offensive towards Jews on his radio talk show <i>The Radio Factor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2004_ADF_letter_to_Bill_O.27Reilly_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-2004_ADF_letter_to_Bill_O.27Reilly-131">[131]</a></sup> The group found issue with his response to the call of a Jewish listener named "Joel", who complained of Christian proselytizing through the celebration of Christmas in public schools, which included O'Reilly stating that:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Overwhelmingly, America is Christian. And the holiday is a federal holiday honoring the philosopher Jesus. So you don't wanna hear about it? Impossible … if you are really offended you gotta go to Israel, then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SunTimes_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-SunTimes-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The ADL responded in their 2004 letter, stating that:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>American Jews are Americans. Jews and other religious minorities are part of America's great tradition of religious freedom. The discomfort with proselytizing, or the intrusion of Christian teachings in public schools, is a very legitimate concern.</p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Books_by_O.27Reilly">Books by O'Reilly</span></h2>
<p>O'Reilly has authored or co-authored a number of books:</p>
<ul>
<li><cite class="citation book">O'Reilly, Bill (1998). <i><a href="/wiki/Those_Who_Trespass" title="Those Who Trespass">Those Who Trespass</a></i>. Bancroft Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-9631246-8-4" title="Special:BookSources/0-9631246-8-4">0-9631246-8-4</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABill+O%27Reilly+%28political+commentator%29&amp;rft.aufirst=Bill&amp;rft.aulast=O%27Reilly&amp;rft.btitle=Those+Who+Trespass&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-9631246-8-4&amp;rft.pub=Bancroft+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Editor, Gabriel Arana Senior Media; Post, The Huffington (March 30, 2015). <a class="external text" href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/03/30/bill-oreilly-lied-falklands_n_6970194.html" rel="nofollow">"Bill O'Reilly Lied About Rescuing Me in Buenos Aires, Says CBS Cameraman"</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABill+O%27Reilly+%28political+commentator%29&amp;rft.aufirst=Gabriel+Arana+Senior+Media&amp;rft.aulast=Editor&amp;rft.au=Post%2C+The+Huffington&amp;rft.btitle=Bill+O%27Reilly+Lied+About+Rescuing+Me+in+Buenos+Aires%2C+Says+CBS+Cameraman&amp;rft.date=2015-03-30&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.huffingtonpost.com%2F2015%2F03%2F30%2Fbill-oreilly-lied-falklands_n_6970194.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-interview2009-falklands-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-interview2009-falklands_77-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation interview">Lemma, Ingrid (September 26, 2009). <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EFMpfy898xM" rel="nofollow">"VVH-TV's "American Dreams Show<span style="padding-right:0.2em;">"</span>"</a> (Interview). <q>O'REILLY: I was down in El Salvador in the 80s, then I went over to the Falklands Island War. Covered from Buenos Aires and Montevideo. Then I went to Israel and covered that. And then I went to Northern Island and covered that. So I've seen the best and the worst and I know the worst. LEMMA: At times dangerous situations. O'REILLY: Yes, it was dangerous. I almost got killed a couple of times. LEMMA: Is there one situation in particular.. O'REILLY: When the Argentines surrendered to the British, there were riots in the streets of Buenos Aires. I wrote about this in my novel <i>Those who Trespass</i>. And I was out there, pretty much by myself because the other CBS News Correspondents were hiding in the Hotel. And I said "why you guys.. you gotta get out and cover the story"..which I did. But, when the riots broke out, in the Casa Rosada, that's where the presidential palace is, people were kind of storming the presidential palace because they were so angry that they have lost face, that they have lost to the British. So there must have been 5,000 or 6,000 people. And the army was standing between the people and the presidential palace. Here in United States we would do tear gas and rubber bullets. They were doing real bullets. They were just gunning these people down. Shoot them down on the streets. LEMMA: So you could have gotten killed. O'REILLY: I was there watching this from about 15 feet away from where the army was shooting. And you got to understand it. When you are in El Salvador, or Argentina or even Northern Island you are on your own. There is no Americans. So when I went to Afghanistan and Iraq, with The Factor, we had guys. We had American guys with us, wherever we were. We were in some dangerous places but we had American soldiers around us. When I was down there, you are by yourself. Nobody is gonna help you. So anyway, when the riots broke out, my shooter, my photographer, got run over by the crowd. Got trampled by the crowd and the camera went flying. I saved the tape, because it was unbelievable tape. But I dragged him off the street. Because he was bleeding from the ear and had hit his head on the concrete. So I dragged him off the street with one hand, and I got the tape with the other hand. The soundman is trying to save the camera, because CBS would not gonna be happy to loose a camera, they are expensive. And then the army comes running down and the guy points the M-16 at our.. And I'm going "Periodista, no dispare" which means "Journalist, don't shoot". I said "Por favor", "Please, don't shoot". I wasn't begging, you beg and you are in trouble.(...)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABill+O%27Reilly+%28political+commentator%29&amp;rft.aufirst=Ingrid&amp;rft.aulast=Lemma&amp;rft.btitle=VVH-TV%27s+%22American+Dreams+Show%22&amp;rft.date=2009-09-26&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DEFMpfy898xM&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
